<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_3bfeafd1-4d63-42e3-9f53-2e8287275f7b'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }
  //]]>
</script>

But Luke doesn't make it easy, and soon everyone—the town, the paparazzi, and the tabloids alike—know his secret...and Jenny is caught right in the middle of all the chaos.</span>

it better not be but idk. The ending is .not it. And i started yelling at the page so.... But i watch starstruck 14 times u month.
</span>
</div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780330433006" href="/book/show/607679.Teen_Idol">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10326079-mishma-nixon?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10326079-mishma-nixon?shelf=ya-contemporary">ya-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10326079-mishma-nixon?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer423658054" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5595650148472838016">Teen Idol was the book which changed my opinion of ‘pink covered books’.After going through a lot of hideously pink covered ‘Mary Kate and Ashley’s and ‘Hannah Montana’s in the library shelves,I was actually disgusted with the colour pink.<br/><br/>So you can imagine my eagerness to read Teen Idol.Note my sarcasm.It was also my first book by Meg Cabot.And from what they say “First impressions are the best ones”,I thought she is one of those authors who write nonsense.<br/><br/>But,boy,I was wrong.Teen Idol was abso</span>
  <span id="freeText5595650148472838016" style="display:none">Teen Idol was the book which changed my opinion of ‘pink covered books’.After going through a lot of hideously pink covered ‘Mary Kate and Ashley’s and ‘Hannah Montana’s in the library shelves,I was actually disgusted with the colour pink.<br /><br />So you can imagine my eagerness to read Teen Idol.Note my sarcasm.It was also my first book by Meg Cabot.And from what they say “First impressions are the best ones”,I thought she is one of those authors who write nonsense.<br /><br />But,boy,I was wrong.Teen Idol was absolutely amazing and Meg Cabot was equally wonderful.Line to line,page to page,this book made me smile.<br /><br />The first thing I loved in this book,was Jen.She was so normal and the kind of a girl,I’ll admire immediately.In fact,in times I saw myself in her.From the way she runs to everyone’s aid to the way he gets along with everyone.she was a lot like me.Well,scratch that ‘like’,I was as if I am experiencing the story myself.<br /><br />Unlike many other books,the hero didn’t grab me.It was not as if I didn’t like Scott,or even Luke for that matter.I liked them both,but not as much as Jen.<br /><br />I enjoyed Teen Idol greatly.It was like going through a personal experience.I had depth.that can be only understood if you think about it twice after you read it.</span>

<div id="review_1333227150" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1333227150" />
    <a title="Fafa&#39;s Book Corner" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7366569-fafa-s-book-corner"><img alt="Fafa&#39;s Book Corner" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588471351p2/7366569.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1333227150?book_show_action=true">Jul 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fafa&#39;s Book Corner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fafa&#39;s Book Corner" href="/user/show/7366569-fafa-s-book-corner">Fafa&#39;s Book Corner</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1333227150" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3290270592313336705"><a href='https://fafasbookcorner.wordpress.com/2016/04/26/review-teen-idol/' rel='nofollow noopener'> Review posted on Fafa's Book Corner </a>!<br/><br/>Beware spoilers ahead!<br/><br/>DNF<br/><br/>I had read this book back in September 2015. I was going through a Meg Cabot funk and I was really excited to read this. Unfortunately I did not enjoy this.<br/><br/>The book begins with a piece from Dear Annie. A girl was having a dilemma with her grandmother. Her grandmother thought that everything said girl had an interest in is going to send her to Hell. The girl has no idea what to do. Annie responds saying that her grandmother is crazy a</span>
  <span id="freeText3290270592313336705" style="display:none"><a href="https://fafasbookcorner.wordpress.com/2016/04/26/review-teen-idol/" rel="nofollow noopener"> Review posted on Fafa's Book Corner </a>!<br /><br />Beware spoilers ahead!<br /><br />DNF<br /><br />I had read this book back in September 2015. I was going through a Meg Cabot funk and I was really excited to read this. Unfortunately I did not enjoy this.<br /><br />The book begins with a piece from Dear Annie. A girl was having a dilemma with her grandmother. Her grandmother thought that everything said girl had an interest in is going to send her to Hell. The girl has no idea what to do. Annie responds saying that her grandmother is crazy and that she's already in Hell, it's called high school.<br /><br />We are then taken to the first chapter in which Jenny is in class. A couple of the boys want to play a prank on their teacher so they steal her favourite doll and go to hide it somewhere. This upsets Jenny because she knows how important that doll is to her teacher. Jenny tries to express her concerns to her best friend (I've forgotten her name). But said best friend brushes it off claiming that the teacher will be fine.<br /><br />That's about as much as I read. I found it surprising that Jenny was nice whenever you interacted with her for example she really did care about that doll, but when she was Dear Annie she was absolutely rude. I know that in media they portray high school as such, and while it isn't rainbows and sunshine, it's not like Hell. I just found that stupid. And yes that girl's grandmother was weird to consider everything her granddaughter liked Hell worthy, that still doesn't mean you have the right to call someone's grandmother nuts. Even if it's true she doesn't right to say that.<br /><br />Overall this was not a good book. I cannot bring myself to recommend this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3290270592313336705" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1806652827" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7371829930988504399">This was every bit of what I expected from Meg Cabot. Yeah, the setup is beyond unlikely and not just the celebrity vising the high school part. But all the unlikely bits make perfect sense in a fun story with people I came to care about and an engaging plot. And, of course, Jenny was a lot of fun to spend time with and joining her while she learns who she wants to be and what she's going to make important in her life was just outstanding. </span>

          </span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5047019-spencer?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5047019-spencer?shelf=2020">2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5047019-spencer?shelf=teen-romance">teen-romance</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1638406952" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2598834692489867244"><b>
  <u>2019</u>
</b><br/>In high school I couldn't get enough of Meg Cabot. And <i>Teen Idol</i> was always my favorite of her books! Reading back through it today, all I can say is, I love it almost as much as I did then! Seriously, the plot is just adorable (and just within the realm of reality/slightly teetering on the unbelievable, but in a really good way). The characters are excellent! Seriously, I want to be friends with Jenny. And Scott. And I've had friends that are exactly like Trina! I did get seriously nost</span>
  <span id="freeText2598834692489867244" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>2019</u>
</b><br />In high school I couldn't get enough of Meg Cabot. And <i>Teen Idol</i> was always my favorite of her books! Reading back through it today, all I can say is, I love it almost as much as I did then! Seriously, the plot is just adorable (and just within the realm of reality/slightly teetering on the unbelievable, but in a really good way). The characters are excellent! Seriously, I want to be friends with Jenny. And Scott. And I've had friends that are exactly like Trina! I did get seriously nostalgia reading this book again and it was amazing.<br /><br />As stated previously, the story itself was amazing. I also loved the Dear Annie additions! I thought it was a great way to show that Jenny did have a little bit more of a personality. Not that I'm dissing on Jenny's normal personality at all! But the Annie letters had a bit more of a bite to them, where Jenny was just straight up nice to everyone.<br /><br />Scott, of course, was a perfect book boyfriend. He was Jenny's friend when he was unavailable/thought she was unavailable. And when he realized they were both available, he was still the same sweet, funny guy he'd always been with her. I loved that nothing changed for him and her, except that they finally admitted their feelings for each other.<br /><br />I'm also super happy (and thought it was super adorable) about Luke and the mystery woman from Clayton High School (if you've read the book then you know who that is and if you haven't then I won't ruin that for you). Also, the whole Trina and Steve romance thing. Honestly, I just loved the whole thing through. All the people and their love lives. It really just puts me back into high school (although, I'm very much with Luke on the whole high school issue. It's basically prison. With worse people. Haha. Except for the people that I cared about, which, in this book, would be Luke, Scott, Trina, Steve, Jenny).</span>
  <a data-text-id="2598834692489867244" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14002639974889433292">Sweet and romantic. I found it extremely satisfying. This is one of those reads when after a tiring day, you just lean back against your couch, prop your feet up on a stool and start to read. It was nice to see that the heroine- a character who always has to be the "nice" person, grow up into someone who can actually take a stand. I found Luke and Scott extremely lovable as well; they're just perfect.<br/><br/></span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_363924018" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/363924018" />
    <a title="Nasty Lady MJ" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4026143-nasty-lady-mj"><img alt="Nasty Lady MJ" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506395877p2/4026143.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/363924018?book_show_action=true">Jul 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nasty Lady MJ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nasty Lady MJ" href="/user/show/4026143-nasty-lady-mj">Nasty Lady MJ</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4026143-nasty-lady-mj?shelf=hollywood">hollywood</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4026143-nasty-lady-mj?shelf=anti-bullying">anti-bullying</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4026143-nasty-lady-mj?shelf=message-read">message-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer363924018" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10263652139028047763">To see full review and Hollywood Analysis click here: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://yalbookbriefs.blogspot.com/2012/07/trend-spotlights-hooray-for-hollywood.html'>http://yalbookbriefs.blogspot.com/201...</a><br/><br/>I often forget about Teen Idol and it's not because it's a bad book, in comparison's to Meg's other titles this one is sort of....well, just there.<br/><br/>The book itself has fairly decent characters and it the storyline is solid enough. But it's nothing special. And perhaps that's what my problem with it is.<br/><br/>The plot is pretty generic, good girl Jen's life is changed when movie star Luke Striker shows up in her</span>
  <span id="freeText10263652139028047763" style="display:none">To see full review and Hollywood Analysis click here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://yalbookbriefs.blogspot.com/2012/07/trend-spotlights-hooray-for-hollywood.html">http://yalbookbriefs.blogspot.com/201...</a><br /><br />I often forget about Teen Idol and it's not because it's a bad book, in comparison's to Meg's other titles this one is sort of....well, just there.<br /><br />The book itself has fairly decent characters and it the storyline is solid enough. But it's nothing special. And perhaps that's what my problem with it is.<br /><br />The plot is pretty generic, good girl Jen's life is changed when movie star Luke Striker shows up in her small town and shakes up things. Honestly, while I am glad that Cabot didn't go the cliche route of having Jen and Luke end up together, I really wondered what Luke's purpose was other than to be a catalyst. Couldn't Jen come up with the conclusion that things in her life weren't perfect? From what was happening in her life before Luke's intervention, I believe she could. But I guess the book wouldn't have sold if he hadn't made an appearance.<br /><br />Also, another big issue I had with Luke was who he ended up with. Geri was a quasi horrible bitchy character. And while it was true she was nowhere near the likes of Lana Weinberger, I still didn't like that all the boys-including Scott-seemed to like her. Especially Luke who seemed to be about seeing someone's natural beauty. Geri just seemed to be this brash kind of bitchy character. She wasn't terrible, but I just don't see her Luke let alone Scott.<br /><br />As for Scott, the love interest in the novel, I didn't like him as much as some of Cabot's other heros. He wasn't awful. He was nice. He cooked. And I liked that, I just felt like I didn't get to know him that well. And while I understand why Jen liked him, I wished their relationship would've been more developed.<br /><br />Things I really did like about this book: the fact that it was a stand alone. While I do like series, it was nice to read something where I didn't have to wait for a sequel. And I really liked how everything was wrapped up in this book. Plus, did I mention it had a nice message that wasn't overly preachy. Yes, that was nice. Plus, did I mention that there's show choir in this book. Yes, all you Gleeks there are some pretty funny show choir scenes in this book which makes me think they really need to bring on Meg Cabot as a consultant for Glee. <br /><br />Best Feature: Not Your Typical Hollywood Story: This book isn't what I expect, meaning I thought Luke and Jen were going to fall in love with each other. No, that didn't happen. And I liked that in a weird way, but at the same time I really had to wonder what was Luke's purpose other than being Jen's Jiminy Cricket. Still though, despite Luke's lack of a role to the story, I liked that it wasn't cliche.<br /><br />Worst Feature: Meh. As far as Meg Cabot novels go, this is a good book. But it's not that memorable. While I think there was a good message in the novel. I just....I wanted something more. I honestly, felt while the foundation was there, there was just something off about the book that it never reached its potential. Perhaps, it was how Luke was handled as a character and for that matter who he ended up with.<br /><br />Appropriateness: This is a pretty clean novel. There is some bullying that goes on in the book, but other than that I can't think of anything remotely inappropriate. In fact, I would recommend this book for teens because of the bullying issues that go on in the book. I love the message this book tries to send without being overly preachy.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10263652139028047763" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_158376526" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/158376526" />
    <a title="Marlee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5214813-marlee"><img alt="Marlee" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/158376526?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marlee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marlee" href="/user/show/5214813-marlee">Marlee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer158376526&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer158376526" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10893421458362221310">Well, I'm hit-and-miss with Meg Cabot. I love love love All-American Girl, but I'm so very disappointed in the premise of the following title that I refuse to read it. The Princess Diaries did not interest me, and Avalon High didn't immediately capture my interest. Anywho, I did not have extremely high hopes for Teen Idol, but I was hoping for a nice little light, predictable teen romance.<br/><br/>It's pretty much just that, but with random messages of social change that are really quite annoying. This b</span>
  <span id="freeText10893421458362221310" style="display:none">Well, I'm hit-and-miss with Meg Cabot. I love love love All-American Girl, but I'm so very disappointed in the premise of the following title that I refuse to read it. The Princess Diaries did not interest me, and Avalon High didn't immediately capture my interest. Anywho, I did not have extremely high hopes for Teen Idol, but I was hoping for a nice little light, predictable teen romance.<br /><br />It's pretty much just that, but with random messages of social change that are really quite annoying. This book makes being "just the nice girl" seem like the worst thing in the world. In order to be a good person, this book claims, you must break whatever rules you don't happen to like, and boss people around. I kind of understood the point Cabot was trying to make, about not being a pushover who's always just fueling the negatives when they're really trying to make things better, but it seemed that the main character was becoming a jerk.<br /><br />Teen Idol is not fully what you would expect if you look at the back cover. I thought the novel would be more about Jenny as an advice columnist on her school paper, and helping the star. Early on, his identity is revealed and the story shifts to the "social change" thing and Jenny's "complicated" relationship with the guy she should obviously be with.<br /><br />Final rant: You know it's bad when a book's syntax is so obvious that it's detracting from your focus on the actual story. Well the story goes a lot like this - with hyphens - all over the place ... and it gets confusing - the story, I mean. (How many times could she use the phrase "I mean"? !!!!!!) I suppose this is part of the character's voice, but it is excruciating to read at times. You should never be struggling to understand a book like this, but at times I caught myself trying to keep things straight simply because it was like a math problem, with parentheses within parentheses within brackets.<br /><br />After all that, I have to say the story had some nice twists and somewhat complex characters. If you like Meg Cabot's stuff, you'll like this. But once you've read one, you've read them all, and I'd suggest that one be All-American Girl, not Teen Idol.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10893421458362221310" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText7896582118803844208" style="display:none">Reviewed by Spreeha for TeensReadToo.com<br /><br />Jenny Greenly has been everybody's best friend or, like her REAL best friend called her, mayonnaise. She even helps out people with them not knowing it's her. You see, Jen is the secret advisor, Annie, who people go to to solve their personal relationships. She does the layout and the other secret thing (being Annie) for the Clayton High School Register in Clayton, Indiana. Of course, only the editor-in-chief of the newspaper and a few other administrators of the school know about the Ask Annie thing. But something very big is about to happen in the small town of Clayton. <br /><br />Nineteen-year-old screen sensation Luke Striker is coming to this town to research a role for a big project coming up. So the school suggested Jenny be the one to show Luke around the school and keep this whole deal a secret. They decided for him to be a transfer student named Lucas Smith. Jen thought that Luke was going to be coming in like a week -- not the very next day! Anyway, Jen is not the type of person who gets star struck by a CELEBRITY! But I guess this was a very first for her. As she got to spend more time with Luke she seemed comfortable around him and didn't think he was one of those people who are just snotty, mean, and self-centered. <br /><br />But will Luke turn out to be someone Jen didn't think he was going to be? Will she blow his cover with a little mistake or will Luke manage to do that on his own? Find out! <br /><br />This book is so awesome! It's just so many things happening that you feel like you're totally in the moment! I personally think that Meg Cabot's books are really good and just right on with the every day life of teens. </span>

<div id="review_2103062439" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2103062439" />
    <a title="Knobby" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9116036-knobby"><img alt="Knobby" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350062174p2/9116036.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2103062439?book_show_action=true">Aug 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Knobby" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Knobby" href="/user/show/9116036-knobby">Knobby</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9116036-knobby?shelf=books-on-kindle">books-on-kindle</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2103062439" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4999731229880912827">(3.5 stars) Okay, this was cute. The story was actually a decent one, and not what I expected when it comes to "celebrity heartthrob goes undercover at local high school and interacts with the normal students" because that usually means that there's a celebrity-falling-for-a-mortal plot. This was refreshingly different! Jen Greenley, an ordinary junior in her small Indiana school, is the anonymous student newspaper columnist Ask Annie. Because she can keep a secret so well, the school administra</span>
  <span id="freeText4999731229880912827" style="display:none">(3.5 stars) Okay, this was cute. The story was actually a decent one, and not what I expected when it comes to "celebrity heartthrob goes undercover at local high school and interacts with the normal students" because that usually means that there's a celebrity-falling-for-a-mortal plot. This was refreshingly different! Jen Greenley, an ordinary junior in her small Indiana school, is the anonymous student newspaper columnist Ask Annie. Because she can keep a secret so well, the school administration asks her to keep some exciting news on the down-low: Luke Striker, 19-year-old Hollywood celebrity, is coming to their small town for two weeks to research a role, and want <i>her</i> to be his student guide. <br /><br />Meg Cabot, unfortunately, sounds the same no matter what. Her Jen Greenley's voice and style is the exact same as Mia Thermopolis of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/38980.The_Princess_Diaries__The_Princess_Diaries___1_" title="The Princess Diaries (The Princess Diaries, #1) by Meg Cabot" rel="nofollow noopener">The Princess Diaries</a>. Her writing is also very conversational, which helps Jen/Mia to sound like a typical 17-year-old, but can be pretty irritating. Probably 80% of her sentences started off with "And" "So" "Anyway" and "But." Still, short cute read, nice palette cleanser before going on to something heavier.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4999731229880912827" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1283693830" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1283693830" />
    <a title="Muse-ic ♬" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36574090-muse-ic"><img alt="Muse-ic ♬" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1497741975p2/36574090.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1283693830?book_show_action=true">May 18, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Muse-ic ♬" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Muse-ic ♬" href="/user/show/36574090-muse-ic">Muse-ic ♬</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36574090-muse-ic?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36574090-muse-ic?shelf=fluff">fluff</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1283693830&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1283693830" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7498365037720922789">2.5. I listened to this on audio and that is not what I didn't like about it. I really enjoy audio books. What I didn't like was the ending....mostly.<br/><br/>I shall now begin ranting.<br/><br/>So I'm a total sucker for books where the snotty stuck-up celebrity/popular person falls in love with the normal-ish everyday main character.<br/>Before you ask, yes that did happen in the book.....but was it with our main character Jenny Greenley? NO!<br/><br/>Was it with some dumb stupid senior girl named Geri who we barely know anythi</span>
  <span id="freeText7498365037720922789" style="display:none">2.5. I listened to this on audio and that is not what I didn't like about it. I really enjoy audio books. What I didn't like was the ending....mostly.<br /><br />I shall now begin ranting.<br /><br />So I'm a total sucker for books where the snotty stuck-up celebrity/popular person falls in love with the normal-ish everyday main character.<br />Before you ask, yes that did happen in the book.....but was it with our main character Jenny Greenley? NO!<br /><br />Was it with some dumb stupid senior girl named Geri who we barely know anything or even care about?! YES! <br />Seriously we don't know that much about her. There was barely any characterization there! She is a senior and she was dating Scott.....the end. Any other facts that I'm missing? NONE! Because there <i>are</i> none to mention.<br /><br />That pissed me off so bad!<br />And that's not the main reason I hated it. WHO THE HELL FALLS IN LOVE OVER THE FREAKING PHONE?<br />Yes people that is <i>EXACTLY</i> what happened.<br />Our beautifully handsome sexy and kind male celebrity Luke Striker was phoning Geri very often to check on Jenny, and then their conversations slowly switched to talking about Geri and then Geri/Luke combo. They fell in love over the phone. <br />Is that not the stupidest romantic outcome ever?! <br />First off, Luke never bothered to associate with Geri before. He always hung around Jenny and mainly talk to Jenny. <br />Geri only "loves" him because he's a hot and sought-after celebrity. There is no way she can fancy herself in love with him, or him her, for that matter.<br /><br />When I heard that part, my eyes went wide. I was so tempting to look at the screen of my Mp3, scream "WHAT?" and risk being dubbed crazy by my family, and chuck the device across the room. On top of that Luke ditched his Spring Fling/Prom date (Jenny). Even if she gave him permission, who does that? finish the night then go get a room with the stupid hormonal senior girl!<br /><br />On to the Scott situation. I can sort of see why Jenny would fall in love with Scott, but he didn't have much characterization either. More than Geri, but still.<br /><br />I think my ranting is over.<br /><br />I find it cool that Jenny is "Ask Annie". I also find it interesting that her personality/outgoingness changed by the end of the book. I liked the change. Except how she was being sort of mean as Ask Annie. She didn't have to switch her hidden and real personas. She could have staying nice and helpful in both....guess not.<br /><br />I am confused by the relevance of the Betty-Ann doll. The Senior Prank? It was an interesting touch but didn't have much importance.<br /><br />The Cara Schlosberg case: sad yet inspiring. Good of Jenny to do some helping in the spotlight instead of behind the scenes.<br /><br />Catrina "Trina". She finally realized that Steve was her "soul mate". <br /><i>only know you love her when you let her go....</i><br />In this case it's "him". It was really mean of her to take advantage of him like that. At least Jenny made her open her eyes. I loved their reunion! It was so cute!<br />I didn't like her "I hate Jenny" episode. At least she came out of it and realized she made a mistake.<br /><br />There definitely could have been more characterization of Jenny's family.<br /><br />I love Luke. Even though his head didn't seem to be screwed on right when he fell in love OVER THE PHONE! <br />Sorry....I will never get over that.<br />He's hot (of course) and he isn't stuck-up. I liked that he actually cared about what happened at Clayton and in high schools in general. <br />It was rather stupid of him to take his shirt off though.<br /><br />Mr. Hall is a self-loving jerk face of a teacher who I don't like. The Troubadours bit was funny. A nice touch.<br /><br />I was liking this book mostly until the end. I didn't hate it, but it definitely annoyed me!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7498365037720922789" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_343328398" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/343328398" />
    <a title="Lint " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8162651-lint"><img alt="Lint " src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/343328398?book_show_action=true">Jun 06, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lint " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lint " href="/user/show/8162651-lint">Lint </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8162651-lint?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer343328398" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6422500450538588726"><i>Dear Annie,<br/><br/>I love him. He doesn't know I'm alive. What do I do now?<br/><br/>Desperate<br/><br/>-<br/><br/>Dear Desperate,<br/><br/>When you figure that out, could you please let me know?<br/>Because I haven't the foggiest idea.<br/><br/>Annie</i><br/><br/><b>
  <u>Jen</u>
</b><br/><br/>Jen's your typical 'girl-next-door.' She's nice, she's caring and she will always be there to wipe your tears. <br/>Jen was, what you would call, a 'goody-two-shoes,' and could get away with a few things.<br/>Luke, a teenage heart throb, and once he got to know her a little, had told Jen that she could make a diff</span>
  <span id="freeText6422500450538588726" style="display:none"><i>Dear Annie,<br /><br />I love him. He doesn't know I'm alive. What do I do now?<br /><br />Desperate<br /><br />-<br /><br />Dear Desperate,<br /><br />When you figure that out, could you please let me know?<br />Because I haven't the foggiest idea.<br /><br />Annie</i><br /><br /><b>
  <u>Jen</u>
</b><br /><br />Jen's your typical 'girl-next-door.' She's nice, she's caring and she will always be there to wipe your tears. <br />Jen was, what you would call, a 'goody-two-shoes,' and could get away with a few things.<br />Luke, a teenage heart throb, and once he got to know her a little, had told Jen that she could make a difference to the school, which happened to lack respect and courtesy.<br />She was on the school newspaper because she was "Ask Annie" and gave advice to those who sent for help. Jen actually had a truthful and trustful nature, maing it easier for people to like her.<br />At times, her advice was funny and I think her responses were pretty good.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Scott</u>
</b><br /><br />Scott's parents split, making him move to another place with his mother. Then one day, he came back to Clayton High, seemingly giving his father a chance, and started to live with him.<br />He's apparently the 'geeky' type and worked at the newspaper thingo as well. He, and a few other staff members, knew that "Ask Annie" was in fact Jen.<br />I actually liked Scott. He was pretty laid back and, to be honest, was way more attractive than Luke.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Trina</u>
</b><br /><br />At first I was like, "WTF, bro?"<br />But then I realised that's how she is. Crazily, overly obsessed with Luke Striker, a guy she will never have.<br />Then I was like, what a son of a bitch.<br />I hated her. I really, really, really, really, really, - words cannot express how much I didn't like her. Trina was a self absorbed, using bitch that used Steve and didn't care for Jen.<br />SMH.<br />But even when she apologised, I still didn't like her. At all. I still don't.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Luke</u>
</b><br /><br />Luke was alright, I mean, I thought he was supposed to be hot? I guess he was but I didn't fall for him one. Tiny. Bit.<br />He was annoying, bossy and confusing. But I liked how he cared for people and cared for 'making a difference.'<br />Yeah...that's all I got.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Overall</u>
</b><br /><br />This book was a light read - I read it in, like, a few hours.<br />I liked Scott, disliked Trina.<br />No, what I liked was when Jen stopped being nice and started being straight forward. I don't know why she wasn't like that in the first place.<br />Anyways, I have no idea why I read this and now I'm going to stop because I have nothing to say...type? Whatever.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6422500450538588726" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9765799694425080468">Rating: 3.5 Stars<br/><br/>I needed a book set in Indiana for my reading challenge, and I thought, Meg Cabot - why not? <br/><br/>I think I started this book thinking it was going to be more about the Hollywood teen idol, Luke, but really, it was Jenny, who was the teen idol. <br/><br/>She had been playing the role of peacekeeper for a long while. They thought of her as the mayonnaise, the one who held everyone together. She often committed acts of kindness, expecting nothing in return, but she was not one to cause any waves</span>
  <span id="freeText9765799694425080468" style="display:none">Rating: 3.5 Stars<br /><br />I needed a book set in Indiana for my reading challenge, and I thought, Meg Cabot - why not? <br /><br />I think I started this book thinking it was going to be more about the Hollywood teen idol, Luke, but really, it was Jenny, who was the teen idol. <br /><br />She had been playing the role of peacekeeper for a long while. They thought of her as the mayonnaise, the one who held everyone together. She often committed acts of kindness, expecting nothing in return, but she was not one to cause any waves. I loved that Luke challenged her to use her influence in bigger ways. She did a lot of brave and bold things at Luke's urging, and it was great watching her take those chances. <br /><br />I also enjoyed some of the references in this story more than I should have. But, seriously, I really miss Chi Chi's. <br /><br />Overall: This book was fun and cute, and I could get behind the overall message.       <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer45778959" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17011432931507855818">Even better than The Princess Diaries series, TEEN IDOL is the story about a girl-next-door who learns to use her influence to change the world. (Okay, not the world. But at least the people at her high school.) <br/><br/>Nice girl Jenny Greenley has a secret position on the school newspaper: she's Ask Annie, the unofficial school psychologist who gives advice to anyone who writes in. Only the school administrators and Scott Bennett, her friend and the newspaper's editor-in-chief, know about her extra job</span>
  <span id="freeText17011432931507855818" style="display:none">Even better than The Princess Diaries series, TEEN IDOL is the story about a girl-next-door who learns to use her influence to change the world. (Okay, not the world. But at least the people at her high school.) <br /><br />Nice girl Jenny Greenley has a secret position on the school newspaper: she's Ask Annie, the unofficial school psychologist who gives advice to anyone who writes in. Only the school administrators and Scott Bennett, her friend and the newspaper's editor-in-chief, know about her extra job. Jenny is good at keeping secrets and not making a big deal out of things; that's why the administration chooses her to be the student guide for Luke Striker, a famous teen actor who's going undercover at Jenny's high school in order to research how normal high school students act for his next movie. If it had been anyone else being the guide, “Lucas’” secret would have been out and at the mercy of the high school’s extremely silly girls, including Jenny’s best friend, super-devoted fan Trina.<br /><br />Through unforeseeable circumstances, Luke's real identity is exposed, and he jets it back to Hollywood--and safety. Before he goes, however, he gives Jenny a challenge: everybody likes her, why not use her power to inflict social change at her high school? <br /><br />Doubtful, Jenny nevertheless tries to speak up more. The results are incredible. She gets Trina mad at her, helps turn a class laughingstock's life around, and stands up for herself for the first time in her life. The only problem is that with her newfound courage, she realizes she might be falling in love…with Scott. <br /><br />As with all of Meg Cabot's books, TEEN IDOL has romance, humor, a bit of ridiculousness, and a happy ending. Jenny is a likeable protagonist, while Scott is a sweetheart. Fans of her other books will by no means be disappointed by this sweet tale.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17011432931507855818" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1664199574" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7004477208606141945">Well. This was pretty.... "Meh" feeling. You know what I mean? <br/><br/>I shelved it under "realistic fiction" but that might be a BIT of a stretch. <br/><br/>I found "teen idol" far fetched and silly. Which might have been the point, but really, I mostly just found it tedious and dull. The romance seemed forced with little chemistry. Both Scott and Luke were ok as far as Young Adult male characters go (so many are creepy stalker asshats) but both were pretty underdeveloped and bland.<br/><br/>Seriously? Why is he called "s</span>
  <span id="freeText7004477208606141945" style="display:none">Well. This was pretty.... "Meh" feeling. You know what I mean? <br /><br />I shelved it under "realistic fiction" but that might be a BIT of a stretch. <br /><br />I found "teen idol" far fetched and silly. Which might have been the point, but really, I mostly just found it tedious and dull. The romance seemed forced with little chemistry. Both Scott and Luke were ok as far as Young Adult male characters go (so many are creepy stalker asshats) but both were pretty underdeveloped and bland.<br /><br />Seriously? Why is he called "sensitive"? He was only doing what any decent person would do, and that was feel bad about those jerks being mean to Cara &amp; Ms. M.... But he still didn't do anything for them did he? He told Jen to do something. Not what I would call sensitive. <br /><br />&amp; if he eats fish &amp; whatever was in that food Scott brought for lunch, then he's not a fucking vegetarian! Wtf? Why even say that? Sorry. I'm a vegan, so this kinda thing really ticks me off.<br /><br />Jen's voice really irritated me. For some who claims to be as well read as her, she sure usually a lot of junk words. Like, you know, I mean. The sorts of words and phrases that teachers always tell you leave out of your essays? <br /><br />Seriously, I almost didn't finish the book because of it. It doesn't read well. <br /><br />And why the hell is she taking Latin and French classes?<br /><br />Was there anything I did like? Well, I did like mentions of famous books and writers. That's always fun. And the dear Annie letters in between chapters were really nice. <br /><br />And the book wasn't Terrible.... Just not great. It was kinda cute, but it was more boring and Annoying then it was entertaining. At least for me. Maybe younger tweener fangirls might enjoy this more, but it simply wasn't for me. <br /><br />I look forward to trying "Avalon high" though. :)</span>

<div id="review_338317610" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/338317610" />
    <a title="Andrea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4653174-andrea"><img alt="Andrea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1498320165p2/4653174.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/338317610?book_show_action=true">May 28, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrea" href="/user/show/4653174-andrea">Andrea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer338317610" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16921397433515421388">Another typical Meg Cabot book. I just don’t like it because it’s so unrealistic and childish. Like a young girl wishing to be with a movie star, the whole princess, fairy tale type thing that I just don’t go for. Meg Cabot is all about these plots that would never happen in real life. How many movie stars would come to somebody’s high school like this?<br/><br/>And the style is writing is the most annoying I’ve ever read. I don’t know if it’s supposed to be funny or what, but having the character say, “I</span>
  <span id="freeText16921397433515421388" style="display:none">Another typical Meg Cabot book. I just don’t like it because it’s so unrealistic and childish. Like a young girl wishing to be with a movie star, the whole princess, fairy tale type thing that I just don’t go for. Meg Cabot is all about these plots that would never happen in real life. How many movie stars would come to somebody’s high school like this?<br /><br />And the style is writing is the most annoying I’ve ever read. I don’t know if it’s supposed to be funny or what, but having the character say, “I mean” after everything she says like we can’t follow a simple sentence is annoying. It’s also insulting to my intelligence. I don’t know if Mag Cabot’s mind works this way or not, like she has to remind herself what she’s talking about constantly, but I can follow along quite easily, and I don’t need to be reminded of <br /><br />It would go something like this:<br />I didn’t want to go to the dance at all. It’s not like they even had good food. So I decided not to go, to the dance I mean.<br /><br />WTH?!?!?!?!?!?!?<br />Why would you have to specify what you were talking about WHEN YOU HAD JUST SAID IT! Does she think we’ve forgotten the topic of conversation in a second’s time?<br /><br />I won’t be reading any more of her books, except maybe the series with Hades if my library gets it in, but otherwise I’m staying away from the rest of her books, with unlikeable characters, bad writing style, barely any of a plot, and unrealistic occurrences with movie stars, actresses, models and every type of fanciful thing that makes for a slightly childish book.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16921397433515421388" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText11697324155056853220" style="display:none">The only reason I continued reading this book when I started it was because I had high expectations...Until I found myself on the last page.<br /><br />The plot BORED me. It was just too predictable. Meg Cabot can come up with such awesome story lines for her books yet decided to make this cliché with no purpose. <br /><br />Time for inconveniences!<br />The only disguise for a superstar who everyone knows is a damn pair of glasses. Sunglasses. What ever. And it works. Wow, just wow.<br /><br />This girl (main character) is well known for her Godly trustworthiness and Teacher's Pet material. So much that teachers give her the job of being this Ask Anne thingy. Which she is bad at.<br /><br />This book would've been so much more better is she told her bestie about Luke Striker/Lucas Smith and then her bestie would tell everyone else.<br /><br />Why did people start calling Cara a cow in the first place? Plot never explained that. The MC is such a popular person. Unfortunately, she is a naive dimwit and cant use her popularity properly. If she did, Cara would've been better ages ago.<br /><br />This random teacher has a mental disorder and is obsessed with a doll. She shouldn't be a teacher without this condition being solved. And she should put her precious doll in a safer place.<br /><br />Didn't anyone think about asking Lucas/Luke about his sunglasses? Ever?<br />Plus, isn't he meant to be paying the MC to keep his identity secret?<br /><br />This book wastes your life. Don't, just don't.</span>

<div id="review_892460791" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/892460791" />
    <a title="Deondra Cherry" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28783302-deondra-cherry"><img alt="Deondra Cherry" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1392829216p2/28783302.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/892460791?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deondra Cherry" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deondra Cherry" href="/user/show/28783302-deondra-cherry">Deondra Cherry</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer892460791" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16913425914236583631"> Meg Cabot’s “Teen Idol” was one of the most relatable books I’ve ever read. In this book Jenny has to try to keep teen star, Luke’s, identity a secret. It turns out this wouldn’t be as easy as she thought. <br/><br/> I’ve never been able to relate to a book as much as I do now. Just like Jenny, I often help a lot of people with their problems. I know how hard it is to keep secrets, that are worth telling. This book is also relatable to “ How to be Popular”, also by Meg Cabot. In this book both of the lea</span>
  <span id="freeText16913425914236583631" style="display:none"> Meg Cabot’s “Teen Idol” was one of the most relatable books I’ve ever read. In this book Jenny has to try to keep teen star, Luke’s, identity a secret. It turns out this wouldn’t be as easy as she thought. <br /><br /> I’ve never been able to relate to a book as much as I do now. Just like Jenny, I often help a lot of people with their problems. I know how hard it is to keep secrets, that are worth telling. This book is also relatable to “ How to be Popular”, also by Meg Cabot. In this book both of the lead characters fall for unexpected people.<br /><br /> In this book the lead female, Jenny, has to help so many people with their problems, that she doesn’t have time for her own. Luke, the lead male, is a childhood star who can’t go anywhere without being mobbed by girls. Just like me, Jenny is a people pleaser. Luke pushes Jenny to change. Jenny has no clue how much power she has.<br /><br /><br /> I highly recommend this book to anyone. If you like usual high school experiences with a twist, then I highly suggest this book. I would give this book five out of five starts, on a scale from one to ten, a one hundred!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16913425914236583631" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christina (A Reader of Fictions)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christina (A Reader of Fictions)" href="/user/show/2602702-christina-a-reader-of-fictions">Christina (A Reader of Fictions)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6571589-teen-idol">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer69444819" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12464985562914175392">Totally held up!<br/><br/>I didn't really remember <i>Teen Idol</i> the way I did a bunch of Meg Cabot's other books, and it's funny because I feel like many of the ones I loved back then I'm not impressed with now, but this one was eh to me when I was a teen and I'm impressed with it now. Cabot does some trope-flipping in this one that I probably couldn't really appreciate when I was less well read but that I now find delightful.<br/><br/>Part of why <i>Teen Idol</i> ages so well is that Jenny Greenley, unlike most of Cabot's m</span>
  <span id="freeText12464985562914175392" style="display:none">Totally held up!<br /><br />I didn't really remember <i>Teen Idol</i> the way I did a bunch of Meg Cabot's other books, and it's funny because I feel like many of the ones I loved back then I'm not impressed with now, but this one was eh to me when I was a teen and I'm impressed with it now. Cabot does some trope-flipping in this one that I probably couldn't really appreciate when I was less well read but that I now find delightful.<br /><br />Part of why <i>Teen Idol</i> ages so well is that Jenny Greenley, unlike most of Cabot's main characters isn't judgmental, so this book does not have the slut shaming that mars many of Cabot's earlier works from a more educated outlook. Luke Striker ends up being different from what you expect him to be, and it's all just very pleasant. A story that easily could have been full of jealousy and hatefulness and is full of healthy relationships, friendship, and kindness instead.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12464985562914175392" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('EITQvDyRtQDhMwtS33jIK7XA1DTPE0WUv2SoThX3pRvR2A51nKL3IPbIKe1GVPDECqZGNdfZIDxowJZI6acZKw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer2864668666710524994">Librarian note: AKA <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/167932.Jenny_Carroll' title='Jenny Carroll' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jenny Carroll</a> (1-800-Where-R-You series), AKA <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/71187.Patricia_Cabot' title='Patricia Cabot' rel='nofollow noopener'>Patricia Cabot</a> (historical romance novels).<br/><br/>Meg Cabot was born on February 1, 1967, during the Chinese astrological year of the Fire Horse, a notoriously unlucky sign. Fortunately she grew up in Bloomington, Indiana, where few people were aware of the stigma of being a fire horse -- at least until Meg became a teenager, when she flun</span>
  <span id="freeText2864668666710524994" style="display:none">Librarian note: AKA <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/167932.Jenny_Carroll" title="Jenny Carroll" rel="nofollow noopener">Jenny Carroll</a> (1-800-Where-R-You series), AKA <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/71187.Patricia_Cabot" title="Patricia Cabot" rel="nofollow noopener">Patricia Cabot</a> (historical romance novels).<br /><br />Meg Cabot was born on February 1, 1967, during the Chinese astrological year of the Fire Horse, a notoriously unlucky sign. Fortunately she grew up in Bloomington, Indiana, where few people were aware of the stigma of being a fire horse -- at least until Meg became a teenager, when she flunked freshman Algebra twice, then decided to cut her own bangs. After six years as an undergrad at Indiana University, Meg moved to New York City (in the middle of a sanitation worker strike) to pursue a career as an illustrator, at which she failed miserably, forcing her to turn to her favorite hobby--writing novels--for emotional succor. She worked various jobs to pay the rent, including a decade-long stint as the assistant manager of a 700 bed freshmen dormitory at NYU, a position she still occasionally misses. <br /><br />She is now the author of nearly fifty books for both adults and teens, selling fifteen million copies worldwide, many of which have been #1 New York Times bestsellers, most notably The Princess Diaries series, which is currently being published in over 38 countries, and was made into two hit movies by Disney. In addition, Meg wrote the Mediator and 1-800-Where-R-You? series (on which the television series, Missing, was based), two All-American Girl books, Teen Idol, Avalon High, How to Be Popular, Pants on Fire, Jinx, a series of novels written entirely in email format (Boy Next Door, Boy Meets Girl, and Every Boy's Got One), a mystery series (Size 12 Is Not Fat/ Size 14 Is Not Fat Either/Big Boned), and a chick-lit series called Queen of Babble. <br /><br />Meg is now writing a new children's series called Allie Finkle's Rules for Girls. Her new paranormal series, Abandon, debuts in Summer of 2011. <br /><br />Meg currently divides her time between Key West, Indiana, and New York City with a primary cat (one-eyed Henrietta), various back-up cats, and her husband, who doesn't know he married a fire horse. Please don't tell him. <br /><br /><br /><b>Series:</b><br />* <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/45023-airhead" rel="nofollow noopener">Airhead</a><br />* <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/43768-the-princess-diaries" rel="nofollow noopener">The Princess Diaries</a><br />* <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/41667-mediator" rel="nofollow noopener">Mediator</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2864668666710524994" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
